On Android, Firebase requires C/C++ and Java components
that are distributed with the Firebase and Android SDKs.

It's likely the required dependencies for Firebase were not included
in your Unity project.
Assets/Plugins/Android/ in your Unity project should contain
AAR files in the form firebase-*.aar
You may have disabled the Android Resolver which would
have added the AAR dependencies for you.

Do the following to enable the Android Resolver in Unity:
* Select the menu option 'Assets -> Play Services Resolver -> 
  Android Resolver -> Settings'
* In the Android Resolver settings check
  'Enable Background Resolution'
* Select the menu option 'Assets -> Play Services Resolver ->
  Android Resolver -> Resolve Client Jars' to force Android
  dependency resolution.
* Rebuild your APK and deploy.

On iOS, Firebase requires native (C/C++) and Cocoapod components
that are distributed with the Firebase SDK and via Cocoapods.

It's likely that you did not include the require Cocoapod
dependencies for Firebase in your Unity project.
You may have disabled the iOS Resolver which would have added
the Cocoapod dependencies for you.

Do the following to enable the iOS Resolver in Unity:
* Select the menu option 'Assets -> Play Services Resolver ->
  iOS Resolver -> Settings'
* In the iOS Resolver settings check 'Podfile Generation' and
  'Add Cocoapods to Generated Xcode Project'.
* Build your iOS project and check the Unity console for any
  errors associated with Cocoapod tool execution.
  You will need to correctly install Cocoapods tools to generate
  a working build.

Firebase is distributed with native (C/C++) dependencies
that are required by the SDK.

It's possible that parts of Firebase SDK have been removed from
your Unity project.

To resolve the problem, try re-importing your Firebase plugins and
building again.

Alternatively, you may be trying to use Firebase on an unsupported
platform.  See the Firebase website for the list of supported
platforms.

Firebase's libApp.so was not found for this device's architecture
in your APK.

A Firebase static library (e.g libApp.a) was not linked with your
iOS application.
